Appendix A.
MALTA.
ORDINANCE No. XI of 1930.
(L.S.)
H. C. Luke,
Officer Administering the Government.
[26th August, 1930.]
Aw Ordinance enacted by the Governor of Malta in the exercise of the powers conferred on him by
His Majesty’s Letters Patent dated the 14th of April, 1921, constituting the office of Governor and
Commander-in-Chief, of Malta and by the Malta (Temporary Government) Order in Council, 1930.
To take a Census of the population of Malta and its Dependencies in the year one thousand nine
hundred and thirtyone.
Whereas in virtue of Section 4 of the Malta (Temporary Government) Order in Council, 1930, the
Governor has full power and authority to make Laws for the peace, order and good government of Malta
by means of Ordinances by him issued in the exercise of the power conferred upon him by Clause 12
of His Majesty’s Letters Patent dated the 14th of April, 1921, constituting the office of Governor and
Commander-in-Chief of Malta;
And whereas it is expedient to take a Census of the population of Malta and its Dependencies in
the year one thousand nine hundred and thirtyone:
It is hereby enacted and ordained by the Governor as follows:
1. This Ordinance may be cited as “The Census (Emergency) Ordinance, 1930”.
2. In this Ordinance, “Malta” means the Island of Malta and its Dependencies.
3. A Census of the population of Malta shall be taken in the year one thousand nine hundred and
thirtyone, on such date as shall be fixed by the Governor and notified by a notice in the Government
Gazette, not less than one month before the date fixed as aforesaid.
4. For the purposes of the Census, the Governor shall appoint a Registrar, whose name shall be
notified in the Government Gazette.
Malta shall be divided into enumeration districts, and as many enumerators and other persons as
may be required for the taking of the Census shall be appointed.
The names of such enumerators and other persons shall be published in the Government Gazette.
Such enumerators and other persons shall, before entering upon their duties, take oath in the form
annexed hereto, before an Officer authorized by law to administer oaths.
5. The Registrar shall, subject to the approval of the Governor, prepare and issue such forms and
instructions as he deems necessary for the taking of the Census.
All expenses incurred, with the approval of the Governor, for the purposes of the Census, shall be
defrayed out of public funds.
6. Schedules shall be prepared under the direction of the Registrar for the purpose of being filled
up by or on behalf of the several occupiers of dwelling houses, in such form or forms and with such
particulars as the Registrar, with the approval of the Governor, may deem necessary.
In this article the expression “dwelling-house” shall include every building and tenement of which
the whole or any part is used for the purpose of human habitation, and where a dwelling-house is let
or sub-let in different apartments and occupied distinctly by different persons or families, a separate schedule
shall be left with or for, and shall he filled up by, the occupier of each such distinct apartment.
For the purposes of this article, a person who is travelling or at work on the night of the Census
day, and who returns to a house on the morning of the following day, shall be regarded as having had
his abode in such house on the night of the Census day,
7. Every occupier of a dwelling-house within the meaning of the preceding article, and every person
in charge of an hotel, lodging-house, school, monastery, convent or other institution, or of any ship lying
in any of the harbours, with or for whom any such schedule as aforesaid has been left, shall fill up the
schedule to the best of his knowledge and belief, and shall deliver the same, so filled up, or cause it
to be delivered to the enumerator when required so to do.


8. Every enumerator shall visit every house in his district, and shall collect all the schedules left
within his district, from house to house, and, so far as may be possible, on the day next following the
Census day. He shall complete such of the schedules as on delivery appear to him to be defective, and
correct such as he finds to be erroneous.
All schedules so collected shall, with all convenient despatch, be delivered to the Registrar.
Every enumerator shall also furnish a return, according to the best information which he is able to
obtain of all the persons present in his district on the night of the Census day, but not included in the
schedules collected by him.
9. The Superintendent, Chief Resident Officer or other Officer in charge of any prison, hospital,
institution or asylum and of any other public or charitable institution which may be determined upon
by the Registrar, shall be the enumerator of the inmates thereof, and shall conform to such instructions
as may be conveyed to him by the Registrar for obtaining, so far as may be practicable, the returns
required by this Ordinance with respect to the inmates.
10. The Registrar shall, subject to the approval the Governor, obtain in such manner as shall ap-
pear to him fit, returns of such particulars as he may deem necessary with respect to persons who, at
the time of the taking of the census, are travelling or on shipboard, or for any other reason were not living
at that time in any house of which account is to be taken by the enumerators, and shall include such
returns in his abstracts.
11. It shall be lawful for the enumerators to ask any questions which may be prescribed in any
instructions issued by the Registrar, and which are necessary for obtaining the information required for
the purposes of the Census.
12. The Governor may make such regulations as he may deem necessary for the taking of the Census.
13. If any enumerator or other person employed under this Ordinance makes wilful default in the
performance of any of his duties under this Ordinance or the regulations made thereunder, or wilfully
makes any false return, he shall for each offence, be liable to a fine ( ammenda ) of not Jess than twenty
shillings.
If any person
1. refuses, or without lawful excuse, neglects to fill up any schedule as prescribed in this
Ordinance, or to deliver the same when required so to do; or
2. wilfully makes, signs or delivers or causes to be made, signed or delivered any false return
of any of the matters specified in any such schedule; or
3. refuses to answer or wilfully gives a false answer to any question necessary for obtaining
the information required to be obtained under this Ordinance;
he shall, for each offence, be liable to a fine ( ammenda ) of not less than ten shillings.
Form Annexed to Ordinance No. XI of 1930.
I* for taking a Census of the population of the Island of Malta and its Dependencies, do
swear that I will make a true and exact enumeration of all the inhabitants within the division assigned
to me, —that I will faithfully collect all other particulars as provided for in Ordinance No. XI of 1930
and in the regulations made thereunder, and in conformity with all lawful instructions which I may
receive; that 1 will make correct returns thereof, as required by the said Ordinance, and that I will not
disclose to any one, except to my superior officers, any information respecting particular persons, obtained
by me and inserted in the schedules.
[Signed)
*lf the oath is taken hy an enumerator , the words u an enumerator” shall he inserted in the blank
left for the indication of the office, if the oath is taken hy any other person employed in connection with
the taking of the Census , the words “an officer” shall be inserted therein.


Appendix B.
Regulations for the taking of the Census of the Maltese Islands in 1931.
GOVERNMENT NOTICE No. 23.
In exercise of the powers vested in the Governor by Article 12 of Ordinance No. XI of 1930, His
Excellency has been pleased to make the following Regulations for the taking of a Census of the
population of these Islands in the year 1931:
1. Commencing from Monday, the 20th April 1931, Schedules shall be left by the Enumerators
appointed by the Governor with, or for, every occupier of any dwelling-house or apartment, and with,
or for, every person in charge of an hotel, lodging-house, school, monastery, convent or other institution
or of any ship lying in any of the harbours, to be filled up by him or on his behalf.
2. The Schedules shall be collected, as far as may be possible, on the 27th April and they must
be ready for delivery to the enumerator on the morning of that day before 9 o’clock.
3. Every Schedule shall contain the information set out in the following paragraph, respecting each
person who had his abode in the house or other place of residence on the night of Sunday the 26th
April. Persons who died before, or w T ere born after midnight, shall not be entered in the Schedule.
4. The following particulars shall be inserted in the Schedule:
i) The name and surname of every person who had his abode in such house or other place of
residence on the night of Sunday the 26th April;
ii) The relationship of each person to the head of the family;
hi) The age and the sex;
iv) The particulars as to marriage, viz:— whether the person is married, a widower or widow, or single ;
v) The place of birth, and in the case of persons born abroad, the name of the country in which
they were born, and the date of their arrival in Malta;
vi) The nationality of every person born abroad;
vii) The profession or occupation:
viii) The particulars as to employment, viz:—w T hether the person works on own account, or is an
employer, or works for an employer:— in the latter case the name and business of the
employer being stated;
ix) Each person’s place of work;
x) The languages spoken excluding Maltese, and whether the person can write in any language
including Maltese.
January 20, 1931.
Lieutenant-Governor’s Office,
The Palace, Valletta. By Command.
H. C. LUKE,
Lieutenant- Governor.


Appendix C.
Preliminary Report on the Census of the Maltese Islands taken on the 26th April, 1931.
Census Office,
86, Strada Forni, Valletta,
2nd June, 1931.
Sir,
I. INTRODUCTION.
I have the honour to present a Preliminary Report on the eleventh Census of the population of
the Maltese Islands. The enumeration took place on the 26th April, and the collection of the returns
was satisfactorily concluded in all parts of Malta and Gozo, and the returns transmitted to the Census
Office, according to plan.
2. The Preliminary Report differs in the following respects from the substantive Census Report to
be issued later. The figures which it comprises are provisional, and relate solely to the number and
sex and to different elements which compose the population. This information it has been possible to
obtain in advance of the main statistical operations by so organizing the work of the Abstractors as to
permit of the simple figures being abstracted from the Schedules and summaries compiled at the Census
Office. It is not anticipated that any material discrepancy is, judging by past experience, to be expected
in the final Census Report.
3. The tables (*) comprised in this Report consist of figures (by sexes) of (al the civilian population
enumerated in each district showing the variation since the preceding intercensal period; (b) the total
population enumerated; and (c) the civilian population enumerated at each Census between 1828 and
1931, showing the intercensal increase.
4. A brief account may conveniently be given in this Report, while the events are comparatively
recent, of the preparations for the Census and of the actual course of its administration.
5. Legislation has, of course, been necessary to confer the powers under which the Census has
been taken. For this purpose Ordinance No. XI of 1930 was published on the 26th August, 1930. In
pursuance of this Ordinance, Regulations were issued by His Excellency the Governor on the 20th January,
1931, (Government Notice No. 23), prescribing the date of the Census (26th April, 1931), the persons by
whom and with respect to whom returns were to be made, and the nature of the particulars to be
furnished in those returns. The Regulations also prescribed the procedure of enumeration.
6. Considerable preparation had, however, been previously necessary. Active arrangements
commenced to be made in July, 1930, when steps were taken in particular to consider the nature of the
enquiries to be adopted. As the Schedule already appeared to have reached the extreme limits of its
capacity for expansion, the problem presented was to decide upon the selection of enquiries which
promised results of greatest general utility for present and future needs. As a result of a process of
sifting, the final contents of the Schedule were settled for submission to the Government and approved
on the 2nd January, 1931. Uor the first time in the history of the Census the Maltese language was
used in the column-headings of the Schedule, together with the English and Italian texts, and although
the trilingual column-headings made the Schedule seen to be a much more formidable document than it
was really, this innovation was of inestimable advantage to that large part of the population who have
no knowledge of either English or Italian.
7. Reference may be made to those respects in which the Schedule adopted differed substantially
from the Schedule of 1921. An enquiry as to place of work, which was felt to bo of great value for
transport purpose was added. On the other hand it was decided to omit the enquiry as to ‘‘infirmities”,
included in previous Censuses, in view of the generally recognized fact that reliable information upon
these subjects cannot be expected in returns made by or on behalf of the individuals afflicted. Further,
it was concluded, after a very careful examination, that the “infant mortality” enquiry could be omitted,
as was recommended in the Census Report of 1921. The necessary data will, however, be obtained from
the records available in the Public Health Department,
8. The administrative procedure of enumeration did not differ substantially from that previously
adopted in recent years. Malta was divided into 105 districts and Gozo into 14 districts; and for each
district an enumerator was appointed to undertake the distribution and collection of Schedules. To each
enumerator was handed an “Enumeration Register and Instruction Book" containing detailed instructions
as regards his duties and responsibilities; and in which all streets and buildings in the district were
entered. This preliminary work was performed by Police Officers, each Officer being selected for his
knowledge of the district, and these entries were thoroughly checked with the sectional Blue Print Map
(*) See Tables I, IV and VII in Census Report.


and Plan of the district before the Registers were delivered to the enumerators. This procedure eliminated
all risk of an enumerator leaving out of the Census any part of, or building in, the district. 1 am indebted
to the Commissioner of Police for his co-operation in lending the services of a number of Police Officers
to prepare the preliminary entries in the Enumeration Registers and in allowing these Officers to act as
enumerators.
9. An acknowledgment of indebtedness is also due to the part played by the Press in the promotion
of a better understanding of the objects of the Census, and a more appreciative reception by the public
of the demands which it makes upon them.
11. STATISTICAL NOTES.
10. The significance of the date selected for the Census lies in the fact that, in the absence of
any express enquiry, in the Schedule, as to each persons normal place of residence, the figures of local
populations must be based upon the residences at which the individuals are enumerated. It follows
that, if the distribution thus obtained is to be taken as substantially equivalent to a classification by
place of normal residence, it must be the aim of the Census authorities to choose a date at which the
movement of the population may be expected to be at a minimum.
11. The first Census was taken in October 1828, and a regular Census was held fourteen years
later in 1842, in March. The next Census was taken in March 1851, and subsequent Censuses
1861-1921 have invariably been taken in March or April. For the present Census the night of the
26th of April was chosen. March or April is generally chosen because the periodical summer movement
of population has not by that time begun and the individual variations recorded (Table 111*) may be
taken as true increases or decreases, as the case may be, of the population in the areas to which they
refer.
12. The total population enumerated in Malta and Gozo on the 26th April, 1931, numbered
258,400; 134,202 being males and 124,198 females. This total includes naval, military and air force
establishments (Table If). The civilian population enumereted numbered 241,621; 117,457 being males
and 124,164 females. In Table 11 § these figures are shown in continuation of the series of corresponding
figures of previous Censuses. It will be observed that the present total is the largest ever recorded and
exceeds the number returned at the previous enumeration of 24th April, 1921, by 29,363 corresponding
to an intercensal rate of increase of 13.83 per cent., as against 10.18 per cent, in 1891, 11.93 percent,
in 1901, 14.52 per cent, in 1911, and 0.33 per cent, in 1921. The increase itself is also numerically
the largest in any intercensal period, while proportionately it is 0.69 per cent, lower than that recorded
13. No comparison can be made between the figures of 1921 and 1931; for owing to the upheaval
caused by the War, and the unsettled period which followed, resulting in the subsequent exodus of
thousands of skilled workmen to the United States of America due mainly to the reduction of the
Dockyard establishment, the increase in the population in the intercensal period 1911-1921 was the
lowest ever recorded, viz : 694 or 0.33 per cent. Conditions have now come down to normal and the
intercensal increase for the period 1921-1931 is again practically on a level with that recorded in
the intercensal period 1901-1911.
14. As in previous Censuses, the Officers and men of local Military corps, the Maltese ratings on
lI.Ms Ships in harbour, and the families of officers and men of the Royal Navy and of the Royal Air
Force, have been included with the civilian population. Wives and children of Army officers and men,
included under “Garrison” in recent Censuses, are for the first time includea with the civilian population.
Thus under the classification “Non-civilian” population (Table I) is shown solely the personnel of the
Royal Navy, the Army and the Royal Air Force, viz: Naval, Military and Air Force serving officers and
other ranks or ratings and “enrolled women”, who have been enumerated in the Census of England
and Wales held on the 26 th of April.
15. The estimated civilian population of the Maltese Islands is given by the Public Health
Department as 234,454 on the 31st December, 1930, and may be taken to have been, approximately,
235,260 on the 26th of April, 1931, (Census Day), This estimate, based on the Returns of Births and
Deaths and of arrivals and departures of passengers is 6,361 short of the actual number of persons
enumerated, viz: 241,621,
16. The discrepancy between the estimated population and the actual enumeration may be attri-
buted to the incompleteness of Returns of passenger statistics, and it is conceivable, therefore, that the
underestimate shown in the Public Health statistical Reports represents th« balance of inward over
outward civilian passenger movement during the intercensal period.
17. The intercensal movement may he analysed into its more important elements as follows; —
Increase —
Births registered in Malta and Gozo ... ... ... (actual) (-f) 75,976
Gain due to excess of inward over outward migration (estimated) (-[-) 4,549
Decrease —
Deaths registered in Malta and Gozo ... ... . . (actual) (—) 51,162
Net intercensal increase (-]-) 29,363
